The Flawed Answer: 'He Did Not Create by Manipulation'
Maturidi critiques an irrelevant answer about God's creation method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi rejects the statement 'He did not create by manipulation' as irrelevant and logically inconsistent.

Core Idea
An answer must address the actual question, not avoid it.

Maturidi examines a theological response and finds it completely off-target. The question was about the 'how' of creation, but the response denied a method that was never implied. This lesson unpacks his critique and reveals the deeper logical principle at stake.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the structure: first a quotation, then a critique, then an elaboration.
The passage is dense. Pause after each sentence.
2
Identify the original question
The question was 'How did He create?' Maturidi points out the answerer misunderstood the question. What was the actual question?
Not 'Did He create by manipulation?' but 'How did He create?'
3
Understand the critique
Maturidi says the answer 'He did not create by manipulation' is meaningless because it denies something that was not asked about. Also, if creation is identical to the thing created, then the answer should mention the thing itself.
This shows a logical error: confusing the method with the essence.
4
Reflect on the principle
The lesson is that theological answers must be precise and directly address the question. Avoid irrelevant negations.
This principle will appear again in later lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله لـ «كيف خلق؟» : «لم يخلق بالمعالجة» وما ذكر كلام لا معنى له؛ لأنه لم يُسأل عما لم يكن، بل سئل عن كيفية فعله؛ فقوله «لم يعالج» لا معنى له، وإذا كان عنده أن خلق الشيء هو ذلك الشيء فليذكر إذا في جوابه ذلك الشيء دون أن يقسم السؤال ثم يُزيل عنه المفهوم من الكيف ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأجاب لمن عارضه بأنه إذا جاز أن تقول: لم يزل عليما سميعا بصيرا لم لا قلت: إنه لم يزل خالقا؟ فزعم أن في ذلك إيجاب الخلق في الأزل. ويعني بـ «لم يزل سميعا» نفي الصمم، ونحو ذلك في العالم والبصير. وزعم أنه يقول: «لم يزل الخالق»، ولا يقول: «خالقا» لما ذكره. قال الفقيه رحمه الله: فإن لم يكن في قوله «لم يزل سميعا بصيرا عليمًا» إلا أنه ليس بجاهل ولا أعمى ولا أصم، فكان التصريح بهذا أولى، إذ هو أبعد من الشبهة؛ إذ قد يجوز أن يقال للشيء: ليس بجاهل ولا عاجز ولا أصم، ولا يجب به الوصف بـ«قادر عالم سميع بصير». فإذا لم يكن في ذا سوى نفي الذي ذكر فحرف النفي خاصة أقرب من حرف
And his statement concerning 'How did He create?': 'He did not create by manipulation' — and what he mentioned is meaningless speech; because he was not asked about what did not happen, but he was asked about the 'how' of His act. So his saying 'He did not manipulate' is meaningless. And if in his view the creation of a thing is that thing itself, then let him mention in his answer that thing itself, without dividing the question and then removing from it the understood meaning of 'how'. And there is no power except with God. And he answered the one who objected to him: if it is permissible to say 'He has not ceased to be knowing, hearing, seeing', why do you not say 'He has not ceased to be a creator'? So he claimed that this would entail affirming creation in preeternity. And he meant by 'He has not ceased to be hearing' the negation of deafness, and similarly for 'knowing' and 'seeing'. And he claimed that he says 'He has not ceased to be the Creator', but does not say 'Creator' for that which was mentioned. The jurist (may God have mercy on him) said: If there is nothing in his statement 'He has not ceased to be hearing, seeing, knowing' except that He is not ignorant, not blind, not deaf, then stating this explicitly would be better, because it is farther from ambiguity. For it is permissible to say of a thing: it is not ignorant, not incapable, not deaf, without it being necessary to describe it as 'powerful, knowing, hearing, seeing'. So if there is only the negation of what was mentioned, then the particle of negation is closer than the particle (of affirmation).
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage contains multiple refutations. First, Maturidi criticizes the answer 'He did not create by manipulation' as irrelevant because the question was about the 'how' (kayf) of creation, not about the method. He also points out inconsistency if one holds creation identical to the thing. Then he addresses an objection: if we say 'He has not ceased to be knowing, hearing, seeing' (which are understood as negations of ignorance, deafness, blindness), why not also say 'He has not ceased to be Creator'? The opponent claims that would imply eternal creation. Maturidi argues that if the only meaning of those attributes is negation, then it is better to state the negation directly, as it is less ambiguous. He notes that saying 'not ignorant' does not automatically entail the positive attribute 'knowing'. Thus, the particle of negation (nafy) is closer to the truth than the particle of affirmation (ithbat) when the affirmation might imply undesirable consequences.

Key Terms
كيف (kayf)
لم يخلق (lam yakhluq)
معالجة (mu‘ālajah)
شبهة (shubhah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that negating a false method (like manipulation) is a valid answer to 'how'.
Correction: Negating what is not implied does not address the question about the nature of the act.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi call the answer 'meaningless'?
A) Because it implies God is a body.
B) Because it does not answer the actual question about the 'how' of creation.
C) Because it uses a non-Qur'anic term.
D) Because it contradicts the consensus of scholars.

Key Takeaway
A proper theological answer must directly address the question posed, not deny irrelevant alternatives.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face difficult questions about God's actions, do you tend to give answers that sound pious but avoid the real issue? What is one area where you have done this, and how can you change that today?
?
Think of a recent conversation about faith where you might have answered a question the person didn't ask. How can you ensure that your words address the actual doubt or need in others?
?
Maturidi calls the answer 'meaningless'. Are there any beliefs or phrases you repeat about God that are actually hollow because they don't engage with the real questions of your heart? Will you commit to examining one such belief today and seeking a truthful answer?

Why Negations Are Preferable for Divine Attributes
Maturidi defends the use of negations against an objection about 'lam yazal khaliqan'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that using negations (like 'not deaf') is clearer and safer than affirmative statements when describing God's attributes, especially to avoid implying eternal creation.

Core Idea
Negations protect divine transcendence better than affirmations can.

An objector asks: if we can say 'He has not ceased to be Knowing' (a negation of ignorance), why can't we say 'He has not ceased to be Creator'? The opponent fears this would imply eternal creation. Maturidi responds by showing that the first set of attributes are actually negations of imperfections, and it is more precise to state the negation directly. This lesson explores his reasoning and the superiority of negative language for God.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, focusing on the objection and Maturidi's response.
Pay attention to the distinction between 'lam yazal sami'an' and 'lam yazal khaliqan'.
2
Understand the objection
The objector says: if we can say 'He has not ceased to be Knowing, Hearing, Seeing', why not also say 'He has not ceased to be Creator'? The opponent's claim is that this would affirm eternal creation.
The objection rests on similarity of phrasing.
3
Analyze Maturidi's explanation
Maturidi explains that 'He has not ceased to be Hearing' actually means negation of deafness, not affirmation of a positive attribute. Similarly for Knowing and Seeing. So the phrase is negative in meaning.
Thus, it does not affirm an eternal action like creation.
4
Grasp the recommendation
The jurist (commentator) concludes that if the only meaning is negation, then stating the negation directly (e.g., 'He is not deaf') is better and less ambiguous. The particle of negation is closer to the truth than the particle of affirmation.
This shows the value of negative theology in kalam.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

So his saying 'He did not manipulate' is meaningless. And there is no power except with God. So he claimed that this would entail affirming creation in preeternity. And he meant by 'He has not ceased to be hearing' the negation of deafness, and similarly for 'knowing' and 'seeing'. And he claimed that he says 'He has not ceased to be the Creator', but does not say 'Creator' for that which was mentioned. So if there is only the negation of what was mentioned, then the particle of negation is closer than the particle (of affirmation).
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage contains multiple refutations. First, Maturidi criticizes the answer 'He did not create by manipulation' as irrelevant because the question was about the 'how' (kayf) of creation, not about the method. He also points out inconsistency if one holds creation identical to the thing. Then he addresses an objection: if we say 'He has not ceased to be knowing, hearing, seeing' (which are understood as negations of ignorance, deafness, blindness), why not also say 'He has not ceased to be Creator'? The opponent claims that would imply eternal creation. Maturidi argues that if the only meaning of those attributes is negation, then it is better to state the negation directly, as it is less ambiguous. He notes that saying 'not ignorant' does not automatically entail the positive attribute 'knowing'. Thus, the particle of negation (nafy) is closer to the truth than the particle of affirmation (ithbat) when the affirmation might imply undesirable consequences.

Key Terms
لم يزل (lam yazal)
نفي (nafy)
إثبات (ithbat)
شبهة (shubhah)
حرف النفي (harf al-nafy)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if you can negate something (e.g., 'not ignorant'), you are automatically affirming the opposite ('knowing').
Correction: Maturidi shows that negation does not entail affirmation; one can negate imperfections without affirming perfections in a way that might imply temporal limitations.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi say 'He has not ceased to be Hearing' actually means?
A) Affirmation that hearing is an eternal action.
B) Negation of deafness.
C) Both affirmation and negation.
D) It is not explained.

Key Takeaway
When describing Allah, negating imperfections is often clearer and safer than affirming attributes that might imply creation or change.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allah is All-Hearing', do you truly mean it as a negation of deafness, or do you subconsciously imagine a human-like hearing that changes with time? How might your heart wander into tashbih without realizing it?
?
This lesson shows that even the phrase 'lam yazal' can be misunderstood. In your own supplications and descriptions of Allah, are you content with simple negations like 'He is not ignorant', or do you insist on affirmative statements that risk ambiguity? What does that reveal about your need to 'define' God?
?
The jurist says negations are 'closer' to the truth and 'farther from ambiguity'. If you were to purify your speech about Allah starting today, which affirmative phrases would you replace with negations? Would that feel like a loss or a liberation?

The Paradox of Creation Being the Thing Itself
Maturidi critiques Ibn Shabib's claim that creating a thing is the thing itself.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's logical critique of the view that creation is identical to the created thing, and why it leads to theological inconsistency.

Core Idea
If creation is the thing itself, then who is the Creator?

This passage from Imam Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid tackles a controversial statement: that God's act of creating is the very thing created. Maturidi dissects this claim and exposes its logical flaws, questioning whether it confuses the Creator with the creature. We will follow his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to understand the flow of Maturidi's argument.
Notice how Maturidi begins by referencing names of exaltation.
2
Identify the key questions
Maturidi poses several probing questions. Locate them and consider what each question targets.
The first question is: 'Is the thing by God's essence or its own?'
3
Analyze the logical consequence
Understand why equating creation with the thing leads to ambiguity about the origin of the thing and blurs the line between Creator and created.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why Maturidi's critique is important for preserving God's transcendence and the distinction between Creator and creation.
This critique defends the Islamic understanding of divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذه أسماء التعظيم والمدح، فكأنه انتفع بالخلق عندهم؛ إذ لم يكن كذلك بذاته فصار كذلك بخلقه؛ جل الله عن صفات الحاجات والمنافع. ولا قوة إلا بالله . قال الفقيه رحمه الله : وقوله : «خلق [الشيء] هو ذلك الشيء»، فإذا الشيء بذات الله أم بذات نفسه ؟ إذ لم يكن من الله إلا ذاته، ولا إلى الخلق منه سوى الخلق بذاته. فكيف صار هو خالقاً ولم يكن منه غير الخلق دون أن كان الخلق بلا غيره؟ ولم لا كان الخلق في أن يكون خالقا أحق منه؛ إذ لم يكن منه إليه سوى أن كان وقدم الشيء لا يوجب كون آخر به هو إذا لم يكن منه إليه ما به يكون في الشاهد كيف أوجب ذلك في الغائب؟
And these are names of exaltation and praise, as if he benefited from creation according to them; since He was not like that in His essence, so He became like that by His creation. Exalted is Allah above attributes of needs and benefits. There is no power except with Allah. The faqih (may Allah have mercy on him) said: And his saying: 'Creating the thing is that thing itself,' then is the thing by the essence of Allah or by its own essence? Since there is nothing from Allah except His essence, and from Him to creation there is only creation by His essence. So how did He become Creator while there is nothing from Him other than creation, without creation being other than Him? And why is creation not more entitled to be creator than Him, since there is from Him to it only that it was, and the pre-eternity of the thing does not necessitate another being through it, since there is from Him to it that by which it exists in the witnessed realm, so how did it necessitate that in the unseen?
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage begins by identifying the names of God as names of exaltation and praise, but then introduces a critical point: Ibn Shabib's claim that 'creating a thing is that thing itself' leads to a paradox. Al-Maturidi asks: if creation is identical to the created thing, then does the thing's existence come from God's essence or its own? Since from God only His essence proceeds, and from Him to creation there is only creation by His essence, how then can He be called Creator? The problem is that if creation is the thing itself, then the thing itself would be the creator in a sense, or God's creative act is not distinct from the creature. Al-Maturidi then argues that in the witnessed world, the pre-eternity of a thing does not make another thing exist through it unless there is a relation from the first to the second. So how can we claim that for the unseen (God)? The passage is a logical refutation of a certain view of creation that conflates the act with the product.

Key Terms
خلق
الشيء
الذات
الأزل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'creating a thing is that thing itself' is a valid definition of creation.
Correction: Maturidi shows that this claim leads to theological inconsistency, as it confuses the Creator with the creature and fails to distinguish between God's act and the created object.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Maturidi, what problem does Ibn Shabib's view that 'creating the thing is that thing itself' lead to?
A) It implies the created thing is pre-eternal.
B) It makes it unclear whether the thing exists by God's essence or its own.
C) It denies God's power.
D) It makes creation impossible.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's logical critique shows that equating God's act of creation with the created thing undermines the distinction between Creator and creature, leading to absurd consequences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If everything in your life, including your very existence, is purely from Allah's creation and not a part of Him, how does that reshape your understanding of your own identity and dependence on Him? What one habit can you change today to live more consciously of that dependence?
?
Maturidi warns against the absurdity of confusing the Creator with the creation. Have you ever attributed to yourself or to someone else a power that belongs only to Allah, even subtly? How will you guard your heart from that error starting now?
?
The passage shows that even a small theological slip can lead to denying the Creator's unique sovereignty. Is there an area of your belief where you have adopted a comfortable but incorrect notion about Allah? What step will you take to correct it, even if it feels uncomfortable?

Refuting Ibn Shabib on the Modality of Creation
Maturidi rejects Ibn Shabib's negative answer as irrelevant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi rejects Ibn Shabib's answer 'He did not create by manipulation' as meaningless and how the question of modality (kayfiyya) requires a direct response.

Core Idea
A question about 'how' cannot be answered by stating what something is not.

Maturidi critiques a theologian named Ibn Shabib who was asked how God creates. Instead of addressing the modality of the act, Ibn Shabib replied with a negation: 'He did not create by manipulation.' Maturidi explains why this answer is irrelevant and fails to address the question. This lesson unpacks the logical flaw in Ibn Shabib's response and clarifies the correct approach to questions about divine acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the question and the problematic answer
Read the first part of the passage where Ibn Shabib is asked 'how did He create?' and responds with a negation. Notice Maturidi's immediate judgment: this is meaningless speech.
The question is about kayfiyya (modality), not about what did not happen.
2
Understand Maturidi's criticism of the answer
Maturidi points out that the answer does not address the question. The question is about the modality of the act, not about what the act is not. He also notes that if creation is identical to the created thing, then the answer should simply name that thing.
Maturidi accuses Ibn Shabib of dividing the question and then removing the intended meaning.
3
Reflect on the proper method of answering theological questions
Consider why it is important to answer directly and not evade. Maturidi implies that a proper answer should affirm something about the modality, not merely negate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله لـ «كيف خلق؟» : «لم يخلق بالمعالجة وما ذكر كلام لا معنى له؛ لأنه لم يُسأل عما لم يكن، بل سئل عن كيفية فعله؛ فقوله «لم يعالج » لا معنى له، وإذا كان عنده أن خلق الشيء هو ذلك الشيء فليذكر إذا في جوابه ذلك الشيء دون أن يقسم السؤال ثم يُزيل عنه المفهوم من الكيف ولا قوة إلا بالله . وأجاب لمن عارضه بأنه إذا جاز أن تقول : لم يزل عليما سميعا بصيرا لم لا قلت: إنه لم يزل خالقا ؟ فزعم أن في ذلك إيجاب الخلق في الأزل. ويعني بـ «لم يزل سميعا» نفي الصمم، ونحو ذلك في العالم والبصير . وزعم أنه يقول: «لم يزل الخالق»، ولا يقول: «خالقا لما ذكره . { قال الفقيه رحمه الله : } فإن لم يكن في قوله «لم يزل سميعا بصيرا عليمًا» إلا أنه ليس بجاهل ولا أعمى ولا أصم، فكان التصريح بهذا أولى، إذ هو أبعد من الشبهة؛ إذ قد يجوز أن يقال للشيء : [ ليس ] بجاهل ولا عاجز ولا أصم، ولا يجب به الوصف بـ«قادر عالم سميع بصير» . فإذا لم يكن في ذا سوى نفي الذي ذكر فحرف النفي خاصة أقرب من حرف يُفهم ما لا منفعة في فهمه، بل فيه كل ضرر .
And his statement regarding 'How did He create?': 'He did not create by manipulation' — and what he mentioned is meaningless speech; because he was not asked about that which did not occur, rather he was asked about the modality of His act; so his saying 'He did not manipulate' is meaningless. And if according to him creating the thing is that thing itself, then let him mention in his answer that thing itself, without dividing the question and then removing from it the understood meaning of modality. There is no power except with Allah. And he answered one who objected to him, saying: if it is permissible for you to say 'He has never ceased to be All-Knowing, All-Hearing, All-Seeing,' why do you not say 'He has never ceased to be Creator'? So he claimed that this would necessitate the creation in pre-eternity. And he meant by 'He has never ceased to be All-Hearing' the negation of deafness, and likewise for the All-Knowing and All-Seeing. And he claimed that he says 'He has never ceased to be the Creator,' and does not say 'Creator' for that which he mentioned. The faqih (may Allah have mercy on him) said: If there is in his statement 'He has never ceased to be All-Hearing, All-Seeing, All-Knowing' only that He is not ignorant, not blind, and not deaf, then stating this explicitly would be better, as it is further from ambiguity; for it is possible to say of something that it is not ignorant, not incapable, and not deaf, yet this does not necessitate the description 'Powerful, Knowing, Hearing, Seeing.' So if there is in this only the negation of what was mentioned, then the particle of negation is especially closer than a word that conveys no benefit in understanding it, rather it contains all harm.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage refutes Ibn Shabib's response to the question 'How did God create?' Ibn Shabib said 'He did not create by manipulation,' which Al-Maturidi dismisses as irrelevant because the question is about the modality of the act, not what it is not. If creation is identical to the thing, then the answer should be that thing, not a negation. Then Al-Maturidi addresses an objection: if we can say 'He has never ceased to be All-Hearing' as a positive attribute, why not also 'He has never ceased to be Creator'? Ibn Shabib claims the latter would imply pre-eternal creation, while the former are mere negations (of deafness, ignorance, etc.). Al-Maturidi criticizes this: if the attributes are only negations, then it would be clearer to state the negations directly, but the formula 'He has never ceased to be All-Hearing' does not merely negate; it implies a positive meaning. The use of the negation particle is better than a meaningless word that brings no benefit.

Key Terms
كيفية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One can answer a question about 'how' something happens by stating what it is not.
Correction: The question demands an explanation of the modality (kayfiyya); stating what it is not does not address the 'how' and is therefore meaningless.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi consider Ibn Shabib's answer 'He did not create by manipulation' meaningless?
A) Because it is a lie.
B) Because it does not answer the question about modality.
C) Because it implies creation is eternal.
D) Because it is a statement of negation only.

Key Takeaway
A proper answer to a theological question must address the specific point being asked, not evade it through irrelevant negations.

The Meaning of Eternal Attributes and Negation
Maturidi critiques the reduction of eternal attributes to mere negations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's critique of reducing eternal divine attributes to mere negations and why such reduction is harmful to theology.

Core Idea
Saying 'He has never ceased to be All-Hearing' means more than just 'He is not deaf.'

This lesson addresses an objection raised against Ibn Shabib: if we can say 'He has never ceased to be All-Knowing, All-Hearing, All-Seeing' as positive attributes, why not also say 'He has never ceased to be Creator'? Ibn Shabib responds by claiming that these attributes are only negations (of deafness, ignorance, etc.). Maturidi and the commentator (al-faqih) refute this reductionism and argue that the positive formulation is richer and more accurate.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and Ibn Shabib's response
The passage presents an objection: if it is permissible to say God is eternally All-Hearing, why not also eternally Creator? Ibn Shabib claims that 'eternally All-Hearing' means only negation of deafness.
This is a key debate about the nature of divine attributes.
2
Understand Maturidi's criticism of reducing attributes to negations
The commentator (al-faqih) argues that if the statement 'He has never ceased to be All-Hearing' only means negation, then it would be clearer to say 'He is not deaf' directly. But the positive phrase implies something more, a positive perfection.
Maturidi insists that the formula 'lam yazal sami'an' is not merely a negation but conveys a positive attribute.
3
Reflect on the harm of misinterpreting divine attributes
Maturidi warns that interpreting attributes as mere negations brings no benefit and causes harm, because it empties them of their positive content and can lead to misunderstanding God's nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Divine Names Are Not Mere Titles: Maturidi's Refutation of Ibn Shabib
Maturidi refutes the claim that divine names are mere titles without attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that divine names like 'al-Khaliq' must be based on real, pre-eternal attributes and do not imply that creation is pre-eternal.

Core Idea
Divine names are not empty titles; they derive from eternal attributes and do not necessitate pre-eternal objects.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi addresses a challenge from Ibn Shabib, who claimed that divine names such as 'the Creator' are mere titles with no real attributes. Maturidi dismantles this view by showing that names are derived from attributes, and that denying the attributes leads to absurdities. He also clarifies that the name 'al-Khaliq' does not imply that creation has always existed, using an analogy with other divine names.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice Maturidi's concise and logical style.
2
Identify the two main arguments
First, Maturidi argues that names imply attributes; otherwise they become impossible titles. Second, he argues specifically about 'al-Khaliq' that it does not necessitate pre-eternity of creation.
These are distinct but connected claims.
3
Understand the analogy with Sami' and 'Alim'
Maturidi draws a parallel: just as 'Sami'' (Hearing) and 'Alim' (Knowing) do not require that their objects (sounds, things known) be pre-eternal, similarly 'al-Khaliq' does not require creation to be pre-eternal.
This analogy is key to refuting the misconception.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this matters: if divine names were mere titles, they could not be pre-eternal; but if they imply attributes, they are eternal. And if 'al-Khaliq' implied pre-eternal creation, it would contradict the temporal origination of the world.
This preserves both God's eternality and the world's creation in time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يُفهم ما لا منفعة في فهمه، بل فيه كل ضرر. ولو لم يرد بذلك سوى نفي الأضداد فليقل: هو صحيح سليم معافى، على نفي الأضداد دون تحقيق الذي ذُكر. فإذا لم يجز ذا بان أن الذي زعم من بيان حاصل الذي ذكر وهم. وبعد، فإن خروج الأفعال المتتابعة على حسن النظام والإحكام هي أدلة العلم بها والقدرة عليها، لا أنها أدلة من ليس بجاهل ولا عاجز؛ إذ غير واحد بما وصفه لا يكون منه فعل ألبتة ولا اتساق، نحو الأعراض كلها. ولا قوة إلا بالله. على أنها أسماء عن صفات تسقط لسقوط الصفات. فإذ لم يُحقق الصفات صيّرت الأسماء أسماء ألقاب، وإذا صارت كذا فالقول بأنه لم يزل كذا كلام لا معنى له، لإحالة اللقب في الأزل. ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم إذ لم يجب في القول بـ «سميع عليم قدير» كون كل معلوم مقدوراً عليه مسمو في الأزل، فمثله في القول بـ«الخالق»، لكن هو خالق الأشياء لتكون على ما هي عليه الآن، كما هو عالم بها كذلك وقادر ونحو ذلك. وإذا كان القول بـ«عالم سميع بصير» وبـ «العالم السميع البصير» واحدا فكذا القول بـ«خالق» و«الخالق» واحد، بل «الخالق» في إيجاب قدم الخلق أحق لو كان التقدير من الملفوظ من «خالق». ألا يُرى أنه على وزن خالق يُقال: ﴿مالك يوم الدين﴾ و﴿خالق كل شيء﴾، يدخل في ذلك كل حادث وقائم، ليس في قوله «الخالق» ذلك، ولا هو يقال عليه في العرف. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
He understands what there is no benefit in understanding, rather in it is all harm. And if by that he only meant negation of opposites, let him say: He is correct, sound, healthy, upon negation of opposites without verifying what was mentioned. And if this is not permissible, then it becomes clear that what he claimed of clarifying the outcome of what was mentioned is an illusion. And moreover, the emergence of successive acts upon good order and perfection are proofs of knowledge of them and power over them, not that they are proofs of one who is not ignorant and not powerless; for none other than what he described would produce any act at all nor coherence, like all accidents. And there is no power except with Allah. [This is] on that they are names derived from attributes, falling with the falling of attributes. For if he does not verify the attributes, the names become names of titles, and if they become such, then the statement that He has not ceased to be such is speech with no meaning, because of the impossibility of the title in pre-eternity. And there is no power except with Allah. Then if it is not necessitated in the statement 'Hearing, Knowing, Powerful' that everything known and empowered and heard [exists] in pre-eternity, similarly in the statement 'the Creator', but He is Creator of things so that they be as they are now, just as He is Knower of them likewise and Powerful and so on. And if the statement 'Knower, Hearing, Seeing' and 'the Knower, the Hearing, the Seeing' is one, then likewise the statement 'Creator' and 'the Creator' is one; rather 'the Creator' is more entitled to necessitate the pre-eternity of creation if estimation were from the uttered [form] of 'Creator'. Do you not see that in the pattern of 'Creator' it is said: 'Master of the Day of Judgment' and 'Creator of everything', which includes every temporal and subsisting thing? Not in His statement 'the Creator' is that, nor is it said of it in common usage. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Ibn Shabib's claim that the divine names, such as Sami', 'Alim, Qadir, and al-Khaliq, are merely titles (alqāb) that do not imply real, pre-eternal attributes. Maturidi begins by criticizing the view that understanding something harmful is useless; he argues that if one only intends to negate opposites, then simple negations like 'correct, sound, healthy' would suffice without affirming actual attributes. He then asserts that the orderly and perfect sequence of actions in the world are proofs of knowledge and power, not merely proofs that the agent is not ignorant or powerless, because without actual knowledge and power no coherent action would occur. Next, he states that names are derived from attributes; if attributes are negated, the names become mere titles (alqāb), and it is impossible for a title to be pre-eternal since a title depends on something else. This shows that the names must be based on eternal attributes. The core argument extends to the name 'al-Khaliq': just as 'Sami', 'Alim, Qadir' do not necessitate that their objects be pre-eternal, similarly 'al-Khaliq' does not necessitate that creation be pre-eternal; rather, He is Creator of things in time. Maturidi emphasizes that 'al-Khaliq' and 'Khaliq' have the same meaning, and if one were to infer pre-eternity from the definite article, then even more so would 'Master of the Day of Judgment' and 'Creator of everything' imply pre-eternity of their objects, which is false. The conclusion is that the names do not imply pre-eternity of what they relate to.

Key Terms
أسماء الصفات (asma' al-sifāt)
الأضداد (al-addād)
الأزل (al-azal)
الألقاب (al-alqāb)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The name 'al-Khaliq' logically implies that creation is pre-eternal.
Correction: Maturidi shows that just as 'Sami'' does not require a pre-eternal object, 'al-Khaliq' does not require pre-eternal creation; the name refers to God's attribute of creating, not to the pre-existence of creation.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why does the name 'al-Khaliq' not imply that creation is pre-eternal?
A) Because 'Khaliq' and 'al-Khaliq' have different meanings.
B) Because just as 'Sami'' does not require a pre-eternal object, similarly 'al-Khaliq' does not require pre-eternal creation.
C) Because the definite article 'al-' indicates something else.
D) Because creation is eternal but not pre-eternal.

Key Takeaway
Divine names are based on real attributes, but they do not necessitate the pre-eternity of their related objects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the name 'al-Khaliq', do you truly believe that He is constantly creating and sustaining you at this very moment? Or is it just a title you say without feeling that reality in your heart?
?
The passage warns against reducing Allah's names to mere titles. Have you ever treated any of His names as just a word without connecting it to His actual attribute? How would your worship change if you saw each name as a direct description of His eternal nature?
?
If Allah's names derive from His attributes and those attributes are real, then His hearing of your dua, His knowledge of your secret sins, and His power over your life are all immediate realities. Does this thought bring you comfort or fear? And how should it change what you do today?

The Witnessed World Points to God's Attributes
Maturidi argues that the witnessed world indicates God's attributes, not His essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the witnessed world indicates God through His attributes, not by directly revealing His essence, and why affirming attributes is necessary.

Core Idea
Creation shows God's attributes, not His essence.

Imam Maturidi explains how the sensible world points to God. He argues that existence after non-existence, variation in states, and consistency all point to specific attributes like power and knowledge. The prophets confirm this. Read on to grasp the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the literal translation. Absorb the flow of the argument.
Notice the three distinct proofs Maturidi offers.
2
Identify the three evidences
Find the three characteristics of the witnessed world: existence after non-existence, variation/gathering of opposites, and consistent order. Each points to a different divine attribute.
3
Understand the conclusion about essence and attributes
Examine why Maturidi says nothing in the sensible indicates an essence without attributes, and why affirming only essence without attributes is invalid.
This counters the misconception that God's essence is directly knowable.
4
Consider the prophetic testimony
Note how prophets, whose truthfulness is proven, describe God with names of attributes (Knower, Hearer, Seer) confirming the argument from creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الشاهد يدل عليه من وجه الشهادة له بالصفة لا من وجه الشهادة بالذات؛ إذ الوجود بعد أن لم يكن هو دليل الإيجاد والإحداث الذي به يعلم الموجود المحدث. واختلاف أحوال الشاهد واجتماع المتضاد في الواحد هو دليل قدرته ونفاذ التدبير الذي بالمدبر القوى يكون، واتساق التدبير، وعدم التفاوت في الواقع تحت العقل على كثرته دليل علم العقل الذي به يُعلم العالم. ولا شيء في المحسوس يدل على ذات إذا نفي عنه الصفة، لم يجز القول بإثبات ذات غير تحقيق الصفات، إذ ذلك غير طريق شهادة العيان. وكذلك شهادة من ثبت صدقهم بالأدلة جاء بالعليم السميع البصير على ذكر العلم والقدرة ونحو ذلك، مع العلم أن هذه الأسماء من أسماء الصفات.
Then the witnessed (al-shāhid) indicates Him from the aspect of testimony to Him by the attribute, not from the aspect of testimony to the essence; because existence after non-existence is the evidence of bringing into existence and originating by which the originated existent is known. And the variation of states of the witnessed and the gathering of opposites in one thing is evidence of His power and effective administration which belongs to the powerful administrator, and the consistency of administration and the absence of discrepancy in what occurs under the intellect despite its abundance is evidence of the knowledge of the intellect by which the world is known. And nothing in the sensible indicates an essence if the attribute is negated from it; it is not permissible to say of affirming an essence without actualizing the attributes, for that is not the way of the testimony of direct observation. And likewise the testimony of those whose truthfulness is established by evidences came with the All-Knowing, All-Hearing, All-Seeing mentioning knowledge, power, and the like, with the knowledge that these names are names of attributes.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage explains that the sensible world (al-shāhid) points to God through His attributes, not by directly revealing His essence. The argument proceeds: existence after non-existence proves an originator; variation and unity of opposites prove power and administration; consistency and order prove knowledge. Nothing in the sensible world indicates an essence stripped of attributes, so affirming God's essence without also affirming His attributes is invalid. Furthermore, the prophets, whose truthfulness is proven, spoke of God as Knower, Hearer, Seer, etc., confirming that these names refer to attributes.

Key Terms
شاهد
صفة
ذات
العيان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's essence can be known directly through creation without reference to attributes.
Correction: The passage shows that creation only indicates attributes; essence cannot be known directly from the sensible world.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, how does the witnessed world indicate God?
A) Directly by pointing to His essence
B) Through His attributes, not by essence
C) Only through prophethood
D) Through negation of attributes

Key Takeaway
The witnessed world testifies to God's attributes, not directly to His essence; thus, affirming attributes is essential for knowledge of God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Proof That God Is Knowing by Essence
Maturidi proves God's essential knowledge from the world's contingent order.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Maturidi proves from the orderly structure of the universe that God's knowledge is essential and not acquired.

Core Idea
God's knowledge is not derived from creation; it is inherent to His essence.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi builds a rational proof for an essential attribute of God. Starting from the established fact that the world is temporally originated, he reasons that its intricate order must come from knowledge. He then eliminates sense perception and analogy as sources of that knowledge, concluding that the knowledge belongs to God's essence itself. This lesson walks through each step of the argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise: the world is contingent
The proof begins with 'ḥudūth al-ʿālam' (temporal origination). Recognize that Maturidi takes this as established. The world did not exist then came to be.
2
Analyze the argument from order
Notice how Maturidi uses 'qiyām al-awāʾil bi-l-awākhir' (preceding things supporting succeeding things) to show the world's order implies knowledge.
This is an inductive argument.
3
Follow the elimination of alternatives
He argues that sense perception and analogy are impossible here because there is no sensed object or precedent. Therefore, the knowledge must be essential.
This moves from knowledge to the attribute of the knower.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : إذ ثبت حدث العالم و محال كونه بعد أن لم يكن على ما عليه من قيام الأوائل بالأواخر واتفاق ذلك علم أنه كان عن علم به. ثم محال كون حس به يُعلَم ولا محسوس أو قياس ولا عبرة، ثبت أنه عالم لذاته. وفيهما العلم لذات العالم سواء غيبة المعلوم وحضرته. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Abu Mansur (may God have mercy on him) said: Since the temporal origination (ḥudūth) of the world is established—and it is impossible for it to be after having not been in the state it is upon, with the preceding [things] supporting the succeeding [things] and their agreement—it is known that it was through knowledge of it. Then, it is impossible for there to be a sense by which it is known without a sensed object, or a measurement without an analogy, so it is established that He is knowing by essence (ʿālimun bi-dhātihi). And in both [cases] knowledge belongs to the essence of the Knower, whether the known is absent or present. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a proof that God is knowing by essence (ʿālim bi-dhātihī). The argument: the world is temporally originated (ḥudāth)—it came into existence after non-existence. Its orderly structure (preceding things supporting succeeding things) indicates it was created with knowledge (ʿilm). Since there is no sense perception or measurement involved in this knowledge (because the world was not yet created), the knowledge must belong to the Creator's essence. Therefore, God is knowing by essence, and His knowledge is the same whether the known object is present or absent.

Key Terms
حدث العالم
عالم بذاته
علم
قياس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's knowledge is acquired from observing creation.
Correction: Maturidi proves that God's knowledge is essential and prior to creation, not derived from it.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi conclude that God is knowing by essence?
A) Because the world is eternal
B) Because the world's order implies knowledge, and no sense or measurement exists
C) Because prophets said so
D) Because God has a brain

Key Takeaway
God's knowledge is essential to His nature, not derived from creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's knowledge is essential and not derived from creation, how does that challenge your tendency to evaluate God's wisdom based only on what you can see or experience right now? Will you trust His knowledge even when it contradicts your senses?
?
The argument says God's knowledge is the same whether the known is absent or present. Where in your life have you assumed that God is unaware of something because it hasn't happened yet? How will you live today with the certainty that He already knows every detail?
?
Maturidi proves that God's knowledge is inherent, not acquired. Have you ever secretly believed that your 'good deeds' or 'bad deeds' inform God's knowledge of you—as if He learns something from your actions? How can you repent from that subtle disbelief and stand before Him as one whose essence He already knows completely?

God's Knowledge: Essential and Eternal
Maturidi argues that God's knowledge is essential and prior.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that God's knowledge of creation is essential and prior to creation, not derived from the objects.

Core Idea
God knows all things by His essence, not through acquisition.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi addresses a fundamental question: Does God know the world because He observes it, or does He know it by His own essence? He argues that since the world did not exist prior to creation, God's knowledge of it could not have come from the world itself. Instead, His knowledge is essential and eternal. Let's trace his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the starting principle
The passage begins by stating that knowledge of God is not derived from sense perception, but from evidence in creation.
2
See how the evidence proves God's knowledge
The created world is made in a way that points to its Maker, showing that God knew it before creating.
3
Refute the idea of external knowledge
Since there was nothing else before creation, God's knowledge could not have come from another source.
4
Conclude that God knows by essence
Therefore, God is knowing by His own essence, not by acquiring knowledge from outside.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : والأصل في ذلك ما ذكرت أنه عُرف لا بالحس، وفيما عرف به دلیل علمه به ؛ إذ جعله على وجه دلّ عليه . ثم لم يحتمل أن يكون علمه به غيره ، لما لم يكن غير حتى أنشأه، ثم ذلك المنشأ كان دليلاً عليه ؛ ثبت أنه كان قبل كونه عالما به، ولا غير له به علم ، ثبت أنه عالم بذاته لا بغيره. والله الموفق.
Abu Mansur (may God have mercy on him) said: And the principle in that is what I mentioned: that it is known not by sense, and in that by which it is known is evidence of His knowledge of it; since He made it in a manner that indicates Him. Then it is not possible that His knowledge of it is from other than Him, for there was no other until He created it; then that created thing was evidence of Him. So it is established that He was, before its existence, knowing of it, and there is no other besides Him with knowledge of it. Thus it is established that He is knowing by essence, not by other than Him. And God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage reinforces that God's knowledge of the world is essential and prior. The argument: the world is known not by sense (since it didn't exist) but by the evidence it provides. The evidence itself indicates God's knowledge because He made it that way. Since there was nothing else before creation, God's knowledge of the world could not have come from another source. Therefore, He knew the world before its existence, and His knowledge is from His essence alone. Hence, He is knowing by essence, not by acquired knowledge.

Key Terms
أصل
عُرف
علمه به
عالم بذاته

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's knowledge is caused by the objects He knows.
Correction: Maturidi argues that since the objects did not exist prior to creation, God's knowledge of them could not come from them. His knowledge is essential and prior.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion of this passage?
A) God learns from creation
B) God is knowing by essence, not by acquisition
C) The world is eternal
D) Sense perception proves God

Key Takeaway
God's knowledge is essential, not acquired, and He knew all things before creating them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
God knew every sin you would commit before you existed, yet He still created you and guides you. How does this reality affect your view of His mercy and your own repentance? Will you come to Him today with a specific failure you've been hiding?

God's Knowledge is by His Essence
Maturidi's logical proof that God knows by His essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's proof that God's knowledge is intrinsic to His essence and not acquired from creation.

Core Idea
God's knowledge is not learned from creation; it is essential to His nature.

Maturidi presents a logical argument to establish that God's knowledge is not dependent on anything external. He starts from the observation that God is known through His creation, but then shows that creation cannot be the source of His knowledge. This lesson unpacks that reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then the translation. Let the argument sink in before breaking it down.
Notice the logical connectors like 'then' and 'since'.
2
Identify key premises
Find three key ideas: God is known not by senses, creation is a proof of His knowledge, and before creation there was no 'other'.
These premises build the argument.
3
Trace the conclusion
See how the premises lead to the final statement that God is knowing by His essence, not by another.
The conclusion is directly stated at the end.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : والأصل في ذلك ما ذكرت أنه عُرف لا بالحس، وفيما عرف به دلیل علمه به ؛ إذ جعله على وجه دلّ عليه . ثم لم يحتمل أن يكون علمه به غيره ، لما لم يكن غير حتى أنشأه، ثم ذلك المنشأ كان دليلاً عليه ؛ ثبت أنه كان قبل كونه عالما به، ولا غير له - غيره - به علم ، ثبت أنه عالم بذاته لا بغيره.
Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The basis of that is what I mentioned: that He is known not through the senses, and that by which He is known is a proof of His knowledge of it; since He made it in a way that indicates it. Then it is not possible that His knowledge of it be through another, because there was no 'other' until He created it; then that created thing was a proof of Him; so it is established that He was, before the coming-to-be of the thing, knowing it, and there is no other besides Him by which He knows; so it is established that He is knowing by His essence, not by another.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a proof that God's knowledge is intrinsic to His essence, not acquired from external sources. Maturidi begins by stating that God is known not through sensory perception but through His creation. The existence of creation itself is evidence of God's knowledge of it. Then he argues that creation cannot be the source of God's knowledge because before creation there was no 'other' entity. Therefore, God must have known the creation from eternity by His own essence. The conclusion is that God is knowing by His essence (dhāt) and not by any external means.

Key Terms
عالم بذاته
علمه بذاته
الحس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's knowledge is acquired from creation or changes over time.
Correction: Maturidi shows that God knew creation before it existed, so His knowledge is eternal and independent of creation.

Checkpoint

A) Because God does not need knowledge
B) Because there was no other entity before creation
C) Because creation cannot be a proof of knowledge
D) Because God's knowledge is limited

Key Takeaway
God's knowledge is eternal and essential to His being, not derived from anything outside Himself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If God's knowledge is essential and not learned, then He knew your sins before you committed them. Does this make you more accountable, or do you feel a false sense of security? What will you change today to align with His eternal knowledge?
?
The passage argues that God knew creation before it existed. How does this truth challenge your habit of worrying about things that have not happened? Will you trust His eternal knowledge starting now?

God's Power by Essence and the Mu'tazila's Contradiction
Dialectical refutation of Mu'tazila on divine power

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite claim about God's essential power and the logical contradiction Maturidi identifies in their view.

Core Idea
God's power cannot be transferred without becoming accidental.

This lesson explores a key debate on divine power. The Mu'tazila assert God is powerful by His essence, not by an accident, yet they also claim He can empower creatures over actions. Maturidi shows this leads to a contradiction: if power is essential, it cannot be removed; if it can be removed, it is accidental. Let's trace the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila's claim and evidence
Start by reading the passage where the Mu'tazila state that God was able to create things before creation, and their evidence from the existence of originated things.
Notice they affirm God's power is by essence, not accident.
2
Identify the faqih's objection
The faqih (teacher) responds by asking: if God is powerful by essence, how can He empower creatures without losing that power?
The key is the consequence of empowerment.
3
Understand the logical consequence
If God empowers creatures, His power over those actions ceases (unless He takes it back). This implies His power is removable, hence accidental, not essential.
This is the core contradiction.
4
See the conclusion
The faqih concludes that describing power as essential yet removable is impossible. Thus the Mu'tazila position is self-refuting.
This shows the importance of consistency in divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم سئل عن الله : أكان قادرًا على خلق الأشياء قبل خلقها ؟ زعم أنه «نعم». دليله أن العاجز ممنوع، فدل وجود المحدث على قدرته. وإذا كان هو قادرًا بذاته، لا بما يعرض من القدرة، فهو موصوف بالقدرة على الدنيا وأمثالها مما لا يحصى. قال الفقيه رحمه الله : } فيقال له : إذ هو قادر بنفسه لا بقدرة يعرض، كيف زعمتم أنه يقدر على خلق جميع حركات العباد وسكونهم إلى أن يُقدرهم عليها ؟ فإذا أقدرهم عليها زالت قدرته عليها إلا أن يأخذ القوة عنهم . فهذا وصف القدرة بالذات أو بالعوارض ومَنْ ذلك وصفه فالقول له بقوة لم يظهر منه الفعل محال ؛ وما يحتمل زوال قدرته فالقول [له] بالقدرة بذاته على مذهبهم محال .
Then he was asked about God: Was He able to create things before creating them? He claimed 'Yes'. His evidence is that the incapable is prevented, so the existence of the originated indicates His power. And if He is powerful by His essence, not by an accidental power, then He is described with power over the world and its likes beyond count. The faqih (may God have mercy on him) said: So it is said to him: Since He is powerful by Himself, not by an accidental power, how do you claim that He is able to create all the movements of servants and their stillness, to the point that He empowers them over them? For if He empowers them over them, His power over them has ceased, unless He takes back the power from them. Then this is a description of power by essence or by accidents, and whoever describes it like that, the statement that He has power by which the act does not appear is impossible; and what has the possibility of the removal of His power, the statement that He has power by essence according to their school is impossible.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical argument concerning the nature of God's power (qudra). The author first presents a Mu'tazilite objection: They ask whether God was able to create things before creating them, and they answer yes, with the evidence that the existence of originated things indicates His power (since an incapable being cannot create). They assert that God is powerful by His essence (bi-dhātihi), not by an accidental power (bi-mā yaʿruḍ min al-qudra). Then the faqih (likely a teacher) responds: If God is powerful by Himself, not by an accident, how can you (Mu'tazila) claim that He can create all movements and stillness of servants such that He empowers them (yuqaddiruhum) over those actions? Because if He empowers them, His power over those actions ceases (unless He takes back the power). This shows that the Mu'tazila description of power is either by essence or by accidents, but if power can be transferred (by empowering creatures), then it is not essential—it would be accidental and removable. The faqih concludes: if power is by accidents, it is impossible for the act not to appear; and if power can be removed, then claiming essential power is contradictory. Thus the Mu'tazilite position is self-refuting.

Key Terms
قدرة (power)
ذات (essence)
عرض (accident)
إقدر (empowerment)
فعل (act)
عاجز (incapable)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God can empower creatures without any change in His power.
Correction: If God's power is essential, it cannot be transferred or diminished. Empowering creatures would remove His power over those actions, making it accidental.

Checkpoint
What is the faqih's main objection to the Mu'tazila view?
A) God is not powerful by essence
B) Empowering creatures would remove God's power over those actions
C) God cannot create movement in servants
D) The Mu'tazila deny God's existence

Key Takeaway
Claiming God's power is essential yet removable by empowering creatures is logically contradictory.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever subconsciously think that God's power is 'limited' by your own choices, as if He cannot handle both His omnipotence and your free will? How does this passage challenge that assumption, and what concrete step can you take today to trust in His all-encompassing power?
?
If God's power is essential and never diminishes, why do you still rely on your own abilities as if they are independent of Him? How can you transform one area of your life this week into complete dependence on His unfailing power?
?
The Mu'tazila fell into contradiction by denying God's power over human actions. Are there areas in your own understanding of God where you hold contradictory beliefs—perhaps thinking He is all-powerful yet not in control of your daily affairs? What would it cost you to submit fully to the Quranic vision of His absolute power?

Refutation of Mu'tazila on Power and Action
Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila claim about power preceding action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam al-Maturidi's refutation of the Mu'tazila claim that power preceding action implies change and temporality, and how he affirms Allah's essential power without change.

Core Idea
Allah's power is by His essence, unlike created power which depends on another and changes.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi directly engages with a Mu'tazila argument that any being whose power precedes its action is necessarily dependent and changeable, implying createdness. He counters by asserting that Allah, exalted, is powerful by His own essence, without any change or dependence. This concise refutation protects the divine attribute of power from anthropomorphic analogies.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the structure: a claim, a refutation, and a concluding remark.
The passage is short but dense; take your time to absorb each phrase.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila claim
The passage begins with 'ثم زعم أن كل قادر سبقت قدرته فعله...' This is the claim Maturidi is refuting. Write it down in your own words.
The claim is that any capable being whose power comes before its action is described as having power through another, leading to change and potential extinction.
3
Understand Maturidi's refutation
Maturidi responds by contrasting Allah: 'فأما الله سبحانه فبنفسه يقدر على الأشياء ويفعلها.' He asserts that Allah is powerful and acts by Himself, without any change or dependence.
This is the core distinction: divine power is essential and immutable.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this matters for tawhid. If Allah's power were like human power, it would imply need and temporality. Maturidi protects Allah's transcendence.
This argument also reinforces that Allah's essence is knowing, as Maturidi mentions at the end.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم زعم أن كل قادر سبقت قدرته فعله، فهو وصف من قدر بغير، وفعله بغيره، فهو يتحول من حال إلى حال، وتقبل ذاته الاستحالة والزوال. فأما الله سبحانه فبنفسه يقدر على الأشياء ويفعلها. فما يذكره في ذلك فاسد، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وقد بينا فيما تقدم بأبلغ من هذا. وبالله التوفيق. وفي هذا آية جعل ذاته عالمة، وقد بينا وهمه.
Then he claimed that every capable (qādir) whose ability precedes his action is described as having power through another, and his action is through another, so he changes from state to state, and his essence accepts transformation and perishing. As for Allah, may He be exalted, He is able by Himself to do things and does them. So what he mentions about that is corrupt, and there is no power except through Allah. And we have already explained earlier with more eloquence than this. And with Allah is success. And in this there is a sign that He made His essence knowing, and we have already explained his illusion.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Mu'tazila claim. The Mu'tazila argued that any agent whose power precedes his action is dependent on something other than himself for that power, and thus changes from state to state, implying temporality. Imam al-Maturidi responds that Allah, exalted, has power by His own essence and acts without any change. Therefore the Mu'tazila analogy is corrupt. He adds that they have already explained this more eloquently earlier, and that in this there is also proof that Allah's essence is knowing (i.e., His knowledge is essential, not acquired), and they have already exposed the illusion.

Key Terms
قادر
قدرة
فعل
استحالة
ذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that Allah's power is similar to human power – it precedes action and depends on something external, implying change in His essence.
Correction: Imam al-Maturidi refutes this by asserting that Allah is powerful by His own essence (bi-nafsihi), not through another, and thus His essence does not undergo change or perishing.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Maturidi, how does Allah's power differ from that of a created being?
A) Allah's power comes from a separate attribute
B) Allah is able by Himself without change
C) Allah's power precedes His action
D) Allah's essence undergoes change

Key Takeaway
Allah's power is essential and immutable; He is powerful by Himself without any change, unlike created beings whose power is dependent and temporal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about Allah's power, do you ever subconsciously imagine it as a 'resource' that He uses to act, rather than as His very essence? What in your daily reliance on Him reveals this hidden assumption? Commit today to reminding yourself that Allah's power is not a tool but His very self, and let that transform your trust.
?
The Mu'tazila argued that change implies imperfection. Have you ever been afraid to ask Allah for a change in your circumstances because you thought it would imply He is inconsistent? How does the lesson that Allah's power is immutable yet actively doing everything (بنفسه يقدر على الأشياء ويفعلها) free you from that fear? Write down one area you have been hesitant to pray about and entrust it to Him right now.
?
If all power is from Allah (لا قوة إلا بالله), then what weakness in your life have you been trying to overcome by your own strength? Will you admit that your inability to change is actually a sign that you need His essential power to work through you? Make a concrete plan to rely on His power, not your own, for one specific struggle this week.

Why Did Allah Create? The Futility of Seeking a Cause
Maturidi answers the question of why Allah created, rejecting causation and redirecting to human duty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam al-Maturidi's argument that seeking a cause for Allah's actions is impossible and diverts from one's own responsibility.

Core Idea
Asking 'why' about Allah's actions ignores that nothing has authority over Him.

This passage tackles a fundamental question: Why did Allah create the world? The Mu'tazila offered an answer based on benefit, but Imam al-Maturidi redirects the entire inquiry. He argues that attributing a cause to Allah is impossible, and that the proper human focus should be on knowing and obeying Allah, not demanding reasons for His actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation carefully. Notice the question, the Mu'tazila answer, and Maturidi's response.
2
Identify Maturidi's first point: cause impossible
Find where Maturidi says 'the notion of a cause is impossible' and understands why: nothing has authority over Allah.
This is a core theological principle: Allah's actions are not subject to external constraint.
3
Identify Maturidi's second point: the question is futile
Maturidi argues that asking about the wisdom of lordship is futile. Our duty is to know Allah and obey Him, not to seek reasons for His actions.
This redirects the focus from speculative theology to practical obedience.
4
Observe the refutation of the Mu'tazila answer
Maturidi points out that the answer 'He created for the benefit of creation' is a deviation because it addresses only a part of creation, not all things.
This shows the importance of comprehensive reasoning.
5
Reflect on the lesson's implication
Consider how this teaching shapes your understanding of divine actions and human responsibility. Why is it futile to ask 'why' about Allah's creation?
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم سئل عن خلقه الأشياء إذ لم يكن له فيه نفع ولا كان عابثًا به، فزعم أنه خلق للعرض على ثواب الأبد؛ وذلك حكمة، فيكون فعله لنفع يكون لخلقه، لا لعلة تقدمت الخلق وهو كإيجاد البنيان وأنواع الأشياء يحدث من العباد. {قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : } وقد بينا نحن ما يقتضي هذا الحرفُ من الجواب. على أن العلة محال؛ لإحالة أن يكون لأحد عليه سلطان، أو يخرج فعله عن الحكمة. وبعد، فإن السؤال عن تعرّف حكمة الربوبية [عبث]. وحق ربوبيته علينا معرفته ومعرفة حقه وأمره، والقيام بما علينا من طاعته وتعظيمه، والإعداد لحق الجواب في كل ما نقوله ونعمله. وذلك يُشغلنا عن طلب الاعتلال له في فعله، أو الاحتجاج بالجواب عنه فيما تعدى السائل طوره، وأعرض عما عليه من أعذاره لفعله الذي هو مسؤول عنه مجزي به. ولا قوة إلا بالله. وقوله : «خلق الخلق لنفع الخلق»، ونفعه ما ذكر، فإنه حَيْد عن الجواب، لأنه سئل عن خلق الأشياء، ومن ذكر فهم صنف من الجملة؛ فلذلك أوجب ذلك حَيْده.
Then he was asked about His creation of things, since there was no benefit for Him in it, nor was He playing with it. So he claimed that He created for the purpose of presenting [them] to eternal reward; that is wisdom. Thus His action is for the benefit of His creatures, not due to a cause preceding creation, and it is like the construction of buildings and various things produced by servants. {Abu Mansur, may Allah have mercy on him, said:} And we have already explained what this point requires of an answer. But [the notion of] a cause is impossible, because it is impossible for anyone to have authority over Him, or for His action to go beyond wisdom. Moreover, the question about understanding the wisdom of lordship is futile. The right of His lordship over us is to know Him, know His right and command, fulfill what is due to us of obedience and veneration of Him, and prepare a correct answer for everything we say and do. That occupies us from seeking a cause for His action, or contesting the answer concerning it, since the questioner has overstepped his bounds and turned away from his own excuses for his action for which he is responsible and will be requited. And there is no power except through Allah. And his saying 'He created creation for the benefit of creation' and its benefit is what was mentioned - that is a deviation from the answer, because he was asked about the creation of things, and mentioning them (a specific group) is a part of the whole; therefore that necessitated his deviation.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage presents a question about why Allah created the world, given that He derives no benefit and is not playing. The Mu'tazila answer is that He created for the sake of rewarding His servants eternally, and that this is wisdom. Imam al-Maturidi responds that the notion of a cause ('illa) for Allah's actions is impossible, as nothing has authority over Him. Then he argues that the very question of seeking a reason for divine actions is futile ('abath). The proper human response is to know Allah, obey Him, and prepare to answer for one's own deeds, not to demand reasons for His actions. Finally, he refutes the specific answer 'He created for the benefit of creation' as a deviation, because the question was about all creation, and answering with a subset (those who will be rewarded) does not address the whole.

Key Terms
علة
حكمة
ربوبية
ثواب
عبث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is permissible and useful to ask why Allah does things, and there must be a reason that we can understand.
Correction: Imam Maturidi teaches that seeking a cause for Allah's actions is impossible because nothing has authority over Allah, and the question itself is futile; instead, our focus should be on knowing and obeying Allah.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Maturidi, why is it problematic to ask for a cause (علة) behind Allah's action?
A) Because Allah acts arbitrarily
B) Because nothing has authority over Allah
C) Because the answer is unknown
D) Because it is forbidden to speak about Allah

Key Takeaway
Seeking a cause for Allah's actions is both impossible and a diversion from our duty to know and obey Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you find yourself more often asking 'why' about your circumstances than asking 'what is my duty right now'? How will you shift your focus today?
?
If the questioner of Allah's actions is described as overstepping his bounds, how does that reshape your attitude when you face trials you cannot understand? What specific action will you take to redirect your mind from seeking causes to seeking obedience?
?
You will be requited for every action you do. Are you truly preparing for that moment, or are you distracted by speculating about Allah's plans? What is one thing you will stop questioning and start acting upon starting now?

The Qadariyya Error and the Principle of Divine Grace
Maturidi refutes the Qadariyya and establishes the principle that all creation shows His grace.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Maturidi rejects the Qadariyya's approach and how the universal manifestation of Allah's grace refutes all questioning of His actions.

Core Idea
Every creature displays Allah's grace and wisdom – questioning them is irrational.

This passage draws a sharp contrast between the misguided approach of the Qadariyya and the sound Sunni principle. Maturidi first points out their error, then lays the foundational rule: all creation bears visible signs of Allah's generosity and wisdom, so any 'why' questions about His actions are absurd.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the shift from critique to positive principle.
2
Identify the two main sections
The passage has a critique of the Qadariyya and a statement of the Sunni principle. Find where each begins and ends.
The word 'وذلك فاسد' marks the critique; 'والأصل عندنا' starts the principle.
3
Understand the aqli vs sam'i distinction
Maturidi says the Qadariyya's answer is scriptural (sam'i), but the initial question was rational (aqli). Grasp why this is a category error.
Rational questions require rational answers, not just scriptural ones.
4
Reflect on the absurdity of questioning
Maturidi lists specific 'why' questions and declares them corrupt. Think about why, given his principle, such questions are inherently invalid.
The principle makes the questions self-defeating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى ذلك شأن القدرية فيما يُسألون عن خلق الأفعال، فيرجعون في الجواب إلى فعل الكفر والمعاصي. وذلك فاسد، لأن طريق هذا سمعي، والأول الذي وصف عقلي. قال الشيخ رحمه الله : } والأصل عندنا أن الله تعالى لم يخلق خلقا إلا وأثر نعمه عليه ظاهر، وأدلة جوده فيه بين، وأن حكمته بما فيه من دلالة وحدانيته موجودة، وبرهان ونفاذ مشيئته فيه محقق، وعلامة قدرته وعلمه بحقائق الأشياء غير خفى في ذلك. والسؤال على أنك لم أنعمت أو لماذا أظهرت جودك، ولم كانت الحكمة، ولم أقمت حجة وحدانيتك ؟ إلى آخر ما ذكر محال فاسد لا يقبله عقل ولا يحتمله وسع لقبحه . لذلك بطل هذا النوع من السؤال. وبالله التوفيق.
And similar is the situation of the Qadariyya when they are asked about the creation of actions; they revert in the answer to the act of disbelief and sins. That is corrupt, because the way of this is scriptural (samʿī), while the first [question] described is rational. The Shaykh, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The principle with us is that Allah, exalted, did not create any creature except that the trace of His grace upon it is apparent, and the proofs of His generosity in it are clear, and that His wisdom in what it contains of evidence of His oneness exists, and the proof and execution of His will in it are confirmed, and the sign of His power and knowledge of the realities of things are not hidden in that. The question like 'Why did you not bestow grace?' or 'Why did you show your generosity?' or 'Why was there wisdom?' or 'Why did you establish the proof of Your oneness?' - up to the rest of what was mentioned - is absurd, corrupt, which no intellect accepts nor capacity tolerates due to its repulsiveness. Therefore this type of question is invalid. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage begins by drawing a parallel with the Qadariyya (those who deny divine predestination of evil) who, when asked about the creation of actions, try to limit the discussion to acts of disbelief and sins. Imam al-Maturidi says that is wrong because that topic is scriptural (samʿī) while the earlier question about creation in general was rational. Then he states the foundational principle of Ahl al-Sunna: every creature without exception displays the effects of Allah's grace, generosity, wisdom, and proofs of His oneness and will. Consequently, any question about why Allah did not bestow grace or why He showed generosity is inherently absurd and unacceptable to sound intellect. Thus such questioning is invalid.

Key Terms
القدرية
النعم
الحكمة
دلالة الوحدانية
سمعي
عقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that questioning Allah's wisdom is permissible; Imam Maturidi declares it repulsive to reason.
Correction: The passage shows that since every creature manifestly displays Allah's grace and wisdom, any question about why He created in a certain way is inherently irrational and corrupt.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Maturidi, what makes the Qadariyya's answer about creation of actions corrupt?
A) They only discuss acts of disbelief and sins
B) They use scriptural evidence for a rational question
C) They deny that Allah creates all actions
D) They claim that humans create their own actions

Key Takeaway
All creation bears witness to Allah's grace and wisdom, making questions about His actions rationally invalid.
